While a constant ("variable") declared with <code>const</code> cannot be reassigned to point to another address in memory (this is an intrinsic property of <code>const</code> regardless of whether it was assigned to an object or a primitive) the additional addresses and values at those adddresses describing an object's properties <em>can</em> change. This is why it is possible to add, remove, or reassign property names and values of objects declared with <code>const</code> but <em>not possible</em> to change the object that <code>const</code> points to.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-variables-as-values-primitives" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#variables-as-values-primitives"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Variables as Values (primitives):</h3>
<p dir="auto">All <strong>primitive</strong> data types in JavaScript (<code>string</code>, <code>number</code>, <code>boolean</code>, <code>undefined</code>, <code>null</code>, <code>bigInt</code>(ES2015), <code>symbol</code>(ES2015)) are known as 'atomic' or <em>indivisible</em> values and are therefore <strong>immutable</strong> (unchangeable). It is impossible to mutate a primitive because what is stored at the memory address of the variable is <em>the value itself</em> (with the exception of Strings, but they are treated as primitive by JavaScript).  All you can do is use the value in an expression or reassign the variable to hold an entirely new value.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-14-printing-vs-returning" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#14-printing-vs-returning"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>14. Printing vs Returning</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-printing" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#printing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Printing</h3>
<p dir="auto"><code>console.log()</code> is sometimes referred to as a 'print statement'.  This method accepts an argument and then prints that argument to the console (the screen in a CLI, or the console in a browser). It is method, so it has a return value: <code>undefined</code>, but that value is not typically useful.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-returning" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#returning"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Returning</h3>
<p dir="auto">All expressions <code>return</code> a value.  This includes <code>variable initialization</code>, <code>ternary operation</code>, <code>function invocation</code>, and <code>arithmetic operations</code> among other things.  A return value is a value which is passed to the calling code at the end of expression execution, in other words, a 'result', and can be used immediately or assigned to a variable for later use.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-15-truthy-values-vs-boolean-values" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#15-truthy-values-vs-boolean-values"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>15. Truthy Values vs. Boolean Values</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-truthiness" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#truthiness"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Truthiness</h3>
<p dir="auto">The concept of <code>truthiness</code> arises out of the <code>implicit coercion</code> feature of JS.  This allows JS to use non-boolean data types in conditions, comparisons, and other operations that expect a <code>true</code> or <code>false</code> value.  We call values <code>truthy</code> that can be coerced to evaluate as <code>true</code> and <code>falsy</code> if they can be coerced to evaluate as <code>false</code>.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-falsy-values" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#falsy-values"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Falsy Values</h3>
<p dir="auto">There are 6 <code>falsy</code> values:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Empty strings <code>''</code></li>
<li>Not a Number <code>NaN</code></li>
<li>All forms of zero <code>0</code>, <code>-0</code>, <code>0n</code></li>
<li>boolean false <code>false</code></li>
<li>Undefined <code>undefined</code></li>
<li>Null <code>null</code></li>
</ul>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-logical-short-circuiting" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#logical-short-circuiting"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Logical Short Circuiting</h3>
<p dir="auto">In certain cases, JS will <code>short circuit</code> logical operations or <em>assume the result based on the first value</em>.  If an <code>AND</code> operation is performed and the first operand is <code>falsy</code>, JS will skip evaluation of the second operands and evaluate to <code>false</code>.  If an <code>OR</code> operation is performed and the first operand is <code>truthy</code>, JS will skip evaluation of the the second operand and evaluated to <code>true</code></p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-the-ternary-operator" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#the-ternary-operator"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>The Ternary Operator:</h3>
<p dir="auto">The <code>ternary operator</code> takes three <code>operands</code>: a <code>condition</code> followed by a question mark <code>(?)</code>, then an expression to execute if the condition is <code>truthy</code> followed by a colon <code>(:)</code>, and finally the expression to execute if the condition is <code>falsy</code>.  This operator is frequently used as a shortcut for the if statement and because it is an <strong>expression</strong> that evaluates to a <strong>value</strong>, its value can be assigned to a variable, unlike the <code>if...else</code> <strong>statement</strong>.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-16-function-definitions-vs-function-invocations" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#16-function-definitions-vs-function-invocations"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>16. Function Definitions vs. Function Invocations</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-function-definition" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-definition"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Function Definition</h3>
<p dir="auto">A <code>function definition</code> contains all of the logic and instructions of a function as well as any parameters it accepts.  It may also name the function (functions <em>can</em> be anonymous).  A function definition does not <code>execute</code> or run the function but it is possible to both define and execute a function using the same expression.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-function-invocation" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-invocation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Function Invocation</h3>
<p dir="auto">A <code>function invocation</code> instructs the program to execute (<code>invoke</code>) the instructions of the function, specifying any arguments to pass to the function at the time of invocation.  This is also called a <code>function call</code>.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-17-function-declarations-function-expressions-and-arrow-functions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#17-function-declarations-function-expressions-and-arrow-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>17. Function Declarations, Function Expressions, and Arrow Functions</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-function-declarations" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-declarations"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Function Declarations</h3>
<p dir="auto">Put simply, a <code>function declaration</code> is any function definition that starts with the <code>function</code> keyword.  Declarations are <code>hoisted</code> to the top of the execution context (scope) when the program is initialized, which means you can call (run) declared functions earlier than the at point where they are declared.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-function-expressions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-expressions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Function Expressions</h3>
<p dir="auto">Any function definition that does not start with <code>function</code> as well as any function invocation is considered a <code>function expression</code>. Common examples are <code>arrow functions</code>, <code>higher order functions</code>, and functions assigned to variables.  Expressions are not hoisted, so they must be declared and defined before they can be invoked.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-18-implicit-return-values" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#18-implicit-return-values"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>18. Implicit Return Values</h2>
<p dir="auto"><em><strong>NOTE: See 07. Arguments &amp; Return Values</strong></em></p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-implicit-functional-return-values" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#implicit-functional-return-values"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Implicit Functional Return Values</h3>
<p dir="auto">An <code>implicit return value</code> is an 'automatic' return value. Functions always return <em>something</em> to the calling code (the <strong>caller</strong>).  If a function does not return a value explicitly (in code), it will always (<code>implicitly</code>) return <code>undefined</code> to when passing control back to the caller.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-19-first-class-functions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#19-first-class-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>19. First Class Functions</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-first-class-objects" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#first-class-objects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>First Class Objects</h3>
<p dir="auto">Functions in JS are <code>first class objects</code> which means that functions can be treated like any other value: they can be assigned to variables, assigned as properties of other objects (<code>methods</code>), and passed to or returned from other functions.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-higher-order-functions" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#higher-order-functions"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Higher Order Functions</h3>
<p dir="auto"><code>higher order functions</code> are functions which are passed to or returned from other functions. In Javascript, functions passed to other functions as arguments are commonly called <code>callbacks</code>.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-function-composition-1" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-composition-1"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Function Composition</h3>
<p dir="auto">Function invocations are valid as both <code>arguments</code> and <code>return values</code>.  When function invocations are passed to other functions as arguments, this is known as <code>function composition</code>.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-20-function-side-effects" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#20-function-side-effects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>20. Function Side Effects</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-function-side-effects" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#function-side-effects"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Function Side-Effects</h3>
<p dir="auto">Operations performed <em>inside</em> of a function that have an effect <em>outside</em> the function without being returned are known as <strong>side-effects</strong>.  There are five categories of function side-effects:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>accessing external interfaces (obtaining user input or logging to the console)</li>
<li>mutating objects in outer scopes</li>
<li>reassignment of a variable in an outer scope</li>
<li>raising an exception without handling it</li>
<li>calling another function that causes a side effect</li>
</ul>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-21-legal-vs-idiomatic-naming" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#21-legal-vs-idiomatic-naming"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>21. Legal vs. Idiomatic Naming</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-legal-names" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#legal-names"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Legal Names</h3>
<p dir="auto"><code>legal names</code> describe the set of characters that are accepted as valid by Javascript when declaring identifiers.  Illegal names will throw errors. All <code>reserved words</code> are illegal for naming.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-idiomatic-names" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#idiomatic-names"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Idiomatic Names</h3>
<p dir="auto"><code>idiomatic names</code> are names by popular convention, for instance, using <code>camelCase</code> for variables and <code>PascalCase</code> for constructors. They are not a requirement, but typically illustrate best practices that have been established such as using <code>descriptive identifier names</code> and <code>avoiding single character variables</code>.</p>
<h2 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-imperative-vs-declarative-style" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#imperative-vs-declarative-style"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Imperative vs Declarative Style</h2>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-imperitive-style" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#imperitive-style"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Imperitive Style</h3>
<p dir="auto">Something is said to be <code>imperative</code> when it is described as a logical set of explicit implementation steps e.g. 'rake the yard starting from the northwest corner to the southwest and moving eastward, in parallel passes 3 meters wide, alternating direction with each pass until finishing in the southeast corner'.  The imperator cares greatly how the task is implemented.  In programming this is often called a <code>procedure</code>.</p>
<h3 dir="auto"><a id="user-content-declarative-style" class="anchor" aria-hidden="true" href="#declarative-style"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M7.775 3.275a.75.75 0 001.06 1.06l1.25-1.25a2 2 0 112.83 2.83l-2.5 2.5a2 2 0 01-2.83 0 .75.75 0 00-1.06 1.06 3.5 3.5 0 004.95 0l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95-4.95l-1.25 1.25zm-4.69 9.64a2 2 0 010-2.83l2.5-2.5a2 2 0 012.83 0 .75.75 0 001.06-1.06 3.5 3.5 0 00-4.95 0l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 004.95 4.95l1.25-1.25a.75.75 0 00-1.06-1.06l-1.25 1.25a2 2 0 01-2.83 0z"></path></svg></a>Declarative Style</h3>
<p dir="auto">Something is said to be <code>declarative</code> when the logic of what needs to be done is separated from the implementation of how its done, with the implementation being unimportant. 'after raking, dispose of the leaves'. It doesn't matter to the declarator how the leaves are disposed of, just that they're gone. In programming this is often called a <code>black box</code>.</p>
</article>
  </div>
